## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Here is the complete map of every Go source file in `grafana/grafana` that participates in the datasource plugin query path, organized by functional layer.

---

## Layer 1 — HTTP Request Handlers (Entry Points)

These files receive the inbound HTTP request and hand it off to the query service.

### `pkg/api/ds_query.go`
The **classic REST entry point** (`POST /api/ds/query`).
- `QueryMetricsV2` / `getDSQueryEndpoint` — authenticates, binds the `MetricRequest` body, calls `queryDataService.QueryData` or `QueryDataNew`.
- `toJsonStreamingResponse` — **response transformation**: converts `*backend.QueryDataResponse` into a streaming JSON HTTP response, setting status codes based on per-refId error sources.

### `pkg/registry/apis/query/query.go`
The **Kubernetes-style API server entry point** (used by the multi-tenant query service and `queryServiceFromUI` feature flag).
- `queryREST.Connect` — implements `rest.Connecter`; returns an `http.Handler` that binds the body, calls `handleQuery`, and wraps the result.
- `handleQuery` — marshals queries into `dtos.MetricRequest`, instantiates an `expr.Service` and `QsDatasourceClientBuilder`, then calls `service.QueryData`.
- `responderWrapper` — **response transformation**: intercepts `Object(statusCode, runtime.Object)` calls to reclassify 5xx downstream errors as 4xx before writing the `query.QueryDataResponse` k8s object.

### `pkg/aggregator/apiserver/plugin/query.go`
The **aggregator API server entry point** for plugin-specific datasource API servers.
- `PluginHandler.QueryDataHandler` — decodes the body, validates datasource UID/type against the URL path, resolves plugin context via `pluginContextProvider.GetPluginContext`, calls `h.client.QueryData`, and wraps the result as `aggregationv0alpha1.QueryDataResponse`.
